### 1390 | 2026-03-16T08:47:27.654911Z UTC / 2026-03-16 08:47:27 +00:00 | human

can my customer support address be a po box for privacy reasons?

---

### 1391 | 2026-03-16T08:47:36.765631Z UTC / 2026-03-16 08:47:36 +00:00 | 055

Yes, a PO box is completely fine for a customer support address. It's a common and accepted practice for exactly that reason — privacy protection — and Stripe has no issue with it.

The one distinction to keep in mind is that Stripe may ask for two different addresses:

- **Legal/payout address** — this needs to be your actual physical US address for identity verification and tax purposes. A PO box typically can't be used here.
- **Customer-facing support address** — this is what appears on receipts and in your support communications, and a PO box is perfectly acceptable.

So use your real address for the account verification side, and the PO box for anything customer-facing. If you don't already have a PO box, USPS offers them starting around $4–$10/month depending on size and location, and you can often set one up online before you're back from Spain.

### 1392 | 2026-03-16T08:48:33.628724Z UTC / 2026-03-16 08:48:33 +00:00 | human

hypothetical question but if i'm temporarily not living in a place with a mailbox can i use a po box as my home address or no?

---

### 1393 | 2026-03-16T08:48:43.425553Z UTC / 2026-03-16 08:48:43 +00:00 | 055

For most everyday purposes yes — a PO box can serve as a mailing address when you're between permanent residences. Banks, subscriptions, general mail, that kind of thing.

But there are a few places where a physical address is specifically required and a PO box won't be accepted:

- **Stripe and most financial institutions** — they require a verifiable physical address for identity and compliance reasons
- **IRS / tax filings** — technically requires a physical address, though in practice many people use a PO box and it rarely causes issues
- **Driver's license / state ID** — requires a physical address in most states
- **Voter registration** — requires a physical address

For Stripe specifically, if you're temporarily without a fixed address, the cleanest options are using a trusted family member or friend's address, or a mail forwarding service like Traveling Mailbox or Earth Class Mail — those give you a real street address that can receive mail and forward it to you anywhere in the world. They're legitimate, inexpensive, and widely accepted by financial institutions because they provide an actual street address rather than a PO box format.

That might actually be worth looking into given you're traveling — you'd have a permanent US address that works for everything and receives your mail digitally.

### 1394 | 2026-03-16T09:25:27.566904Z UTC / 2026-03-16 09:25:27 +00:00 | human

what's the difference in charge timing on stripe

---

### 1395 | 2026-03-16T09:25:45.115066Z UTC / 2026-03-16 09:25:45 +00:00 | 055

Stripe gives you two main options for when to charge customers:

**Charge immediately** — the customer's card is charged the moment they subscribe. Their billing cycle starts that day and renews on the same date each month. Most straightforward, best for cash flow.

**Charge at end of trial** — you give customers a free trial period (you set the length), and the first charge hits when the trial ends. Good for conversion but you're delivering value before collecting payment.

For a subscription product like SoulMode there's also a nuance around **billing cycle timing**:

- **Per-calendar-month** — everyone's bill resets on the 1st regardless of when they signed up. Simpler for tracking usage limits like your 5 generates/month for Pro.
- **Per-billing-anniversary** — each customer's cycle resets on the day they signed up. So someone who joined March 15 resets on April 15. More common default in Stripe.

This matters for you specifically because your Pro tier has a monthly generate limit. You'll want to decide whether "month" means calendar month or billing anniversary, and make sure your Supabase usage tracking logic matches whichever Stripe uses.

The simplest approach for your build is billing anniversary (Stripe's default) and tying the generate count reset to the Stripe subscription renewal event via webhook rather than a calendar date. That way they stay in sync automatically.

---

### 1396 | 2026-03-16T09:26:26.314817Z UTC / 2026-03-16 09:26:26 +00:00 | human

it has options like "invoice prorations immediately at the time of the update" and the other option is at the end of the billing period

---

### 1397 | 2026-03-16T09:26:39.513287Z UTC / 2026-03-16 09:26:39 +00:00 | 055

This is specifically about **proration** — what happens when a customer upgrades or downgrades mid-cycle.

**Invoice prorations immediately** — if someone upgrades from Pro to Elite on day 15 of their billing cycle, Stripe calculates what they owe for the remaining half-month at the new price, subtracts what they already paid, and charges the difference right away. The customer pays instantly when they change plans.

**At end of billing period** — the proration adjustment gets added to their next invoice instead. No immediate charge on upgrade, it all settles at renewal.

For SoulMode I'd recommend **immediately**, for a few reasons:

- It's cleaner for the customer — they know exactly what they're paying and when
- Access to Elite features (like the live test drive) should logically unlock the moment they pay for it, not at the end of their cycle
- It's the standard expectation for SaaS upgrades — people expect to pay when they upgrade and get access right away
- Downgrades are less common and the math still works the same way in reverse

The "end of billing period" option makes more sense for businesses where plan changes are frequent and complex, or where you want to avoid lots of small mid-cycle charges. That's not really your situation.

So: **invoice prorations immediately** is the right call for you.

---

### 1398 | 2026-03-16T09:28:15.592840Z UTC / 2026-03-16 09:28:15 +00:00 | human

for downgrades what does this mean "Note that updating at the end of the billing period requires your integration to support subscription schedules."

---

### 1399 | 2026-03-16T09:28:28.649953Z UTC / 2026-03-16 09:28:28 +00:00 | 055

It means that if you want downgrades to take effect at the end of the billing period (rather than immediately), Stripe can't handle that with a simple subscription update — it requires a more advanced feature called **subscription schedules**, which is essentially a queued future change that Stripe executes automatically at the right time.

Without subscription schedules, a downgrade would apply immediately just like an upgrade, which may not be what you want — you'd arguably want someone who downgrades from Elite to Pro to keep Elite access until their paid period ends.

**Practically speaking for you:**

This is a complexity you don't need to solve right now. The simplest approach for your initial build is:

- **Upgrades:** immediate, charge the proration now, unlock features instantly
- **Downgrades:** also immediate in terms of Stripe processing, but you handle the access gracefully in your app — meaning when someone downgrades you don't strip their current tier access until the next billing cycle starts

That last part is a product decision you control in Supabase, not a Stripe setting. You just don't update the tier in your database until the renewal webhook fires. Stripe doesn't care what access you grant in your app — it just handles the billing.

So the short answer: ignore subscription schedules for now. Handle downgrade access gracefully in your own logic and keep Stripe simple. You can add scheduling later if it becomes necessary.

---
